In addition to ordering the special financial commissioner of Hebei to comply, this reply is for your information.

Circumstances of Guangdong Compatriots Raising Relief for Flood Disaster

This time, torrential floods occurred in the East, West, and North Rivers of Guangdong, causing a major disaster. Yesterday, the United Guangdong Chamber of Commerce in this city received a telegram from Guangzhou Convenient Hospital stating that Chen Bingqian, Cai Chang, and Jian of Shanghai Daxin Company, regarding the North River flood disaster in Lian, Ying, Qing, Si, San, Nan, and Hua counties, had caused over a hundred breached embankments and widespread suffering among the people, more tragic than in the year of Yimao. The provincial capital and cities were slightly less affected. Our hospital initiated an emergency relief effort on the 4th, and by the 14th, united with various sectors to establish the Guangdong Flood Relief Association. Respectfully, Chen Huipu of Guangzhou Convenient Hospital. Furthermore, a telegram from the Tung Wah Hospital in Hong Kong stated, "To the United Guangdong Chamber of Commerce, your telegram received. The Guangdong flood disaster is severe, the affected area is vast, and the cries of the suffering are everywhere, urgently awaiting relief. We have repeatedly organized emergency relief efforts, led by our hospital and the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce. Please raise funds for relief to save the survivors." From Xiao of the Tung Wah Hospital in Hong Kong, etc. At that time, the chairman of the association, Chen Bingqian, happened to be in Mogan Mountain. Upon receiving the telegram, he rushed back and immediately convened a meeting of fellow townsmen to initiate a fundraising association. In addition to the association advancing a large sum of money to Guangdong for emergency relief, Chen Bingqian also donated 5,000 yuan. Donation booklets have been printed and distributed to various sectors. Furthermore, the Shanghai Guangdong merchants' miscellaneous grain industry Shenshoutang, import and export industry Yuanantang, sugar and grocery industry Guangantang, leather industry Shenantang, cotton yarn industry Mianantang, silk and cloth industry association, and major companies are conducting fundraising efforts separately, which is extremely enthusiastic. It was also resolved by the public to designate the Guangdong Bank, Guohua Bank, Sincere, Wing On, and Sun Sun companies in this city as agencies for receiving relief funds.

The Guangzhao Public Association received a telegram from Lu Jingke and Chen Huipu yesterday, appealing for relief. "To Chen Bingqian and Cai Chang of Daxin Company, forwarded to the Guangzhao Public Association, Guangdong Merchants' Hospital, China Foreign Famine Relief Committee, General Chamber of Commerce, and newspaper offices: This flood disaster, originating from a mountain collapse in Lianzhou, has cascaded downstream, with a vast area and deep disaster. Our hospital initiated an emergency relief effort on the 4th, and efforts have continued until the 14th, uniting with various sectors to establish a relief association. We appeal for assistance in raising relief funds." Respectfully, Lu Jingke and Chen Huipu of Convenient Hospital.

The Donggang Steamer is Still Not Out of Danger

▲Passengers Carried from Vientiane to Fujian

▲Shanghai Shipowners' Rescue Measures

The Donggang steamer of the Donggang Company, which encountered an accident near the Sibaiyida Island lighthouse off the coast of Fuzhou, was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, the reporter went to the shipowner Mr. Zhao's residence to inquire about the details of the incident and the current situation, which are further described below.

▲Main Cause of the Accident: The Donggang steamer was recently rented out by the shipowner Mr. Zhao to the Yadong Company in this city, operating along the Shanghai-Fuzhou-Xinghua-Quanzhou route. Last Saturday, the steamer departed from Shanghai to Fujian with cargo. Approximately forty passengers disembarked in Shanghai. According to the schedule, it should have arrived in Quanzhou on the morning of the 21st. However, when it reached the waters off Sibaiyida Island, near Shuangfeng, the steam engine in the engine room suddenly exploded, and the boiler was also damaged. Furthermore, the hull in the middle cabin was cracked, and the machinery was completely damaged, rendering it unable to move. Seawater rushed into the ship. The shipmaster, Sun Quanshun, urgently sent out a distress signal. At four o'clock in the morning on the 20th, it was first spotted by the Japanese ship Lushanmaru. After repeated requests from shipmaster Sun, the Japanese ship only agreed to rescue the passengers on board and transport them to Xiamen. Therefore, Sun Quanshun immediately sent a telegram to Shanghai, stating, "The Donggang steamer encountered an accident near the lighthouse with a ruptured boiler, taking in four feet of water. The engine room in the cabin is extremely dangerous, and the ship may sink. All passengers have been rescued by the Japanese ship. Currently, we are entrusting the ship to tow it, and negotiations are underway."

▲Vientiane Provides Assistance: After the Donggang steamer encountered the accident, in order to ensure the safety of the passengers, it was agreed with the Japanese ship to first send the forty passengers onto the Japanese ship. Then, shipmaster Sun Quanshun requested the Lushanmaru to tow the Donggang steamer to the nearby Huyang Bay beach. However, the Japanese ship firmly refused. Until yesterday, a telegram reported that the Donggang had already been flooded and that towing was impossible. Fortunately, the Sanbei Company's Vientiane steamer, en route from Shanghai to Fujian, heard the alarm and went to rescue. When the Vientiane arrived, the Donggang had already taken in a lot of water and could not be towed further. Therefore, it sent a telegram to Shanghai, requesting the Shanghai shipowners to quickly dispatch tugboats for rescue.

▲Passengers Rescued to Fujian: The forty passengers rescued by the Japanese ship, and after the arrival of the Vientiane steamer, all passengers requested the Vientiane steamer to rescue them to Fuzhou. The owner of the Vientiane steamer, Mr. Liu, immediately agreed and negotiated with the owner of the Lushanmaru. The Vientiane lowered a sampan to the side of the Japanese ship and transferred all the passengers to this ship. Originally intending to send them to Xiamen, it has now been changed to Fuzhou. Yesterday, Shanghai received a telegram from Fujian stating that all those rescued have safely arrived in Fuzhou.

▲Ship Still Not Out of Danger: Mr. Zhao previously received a telegram from Fuzhou stating that the Donggang had been towed to Fuzhou. This telegram was very strange. The shipowner immediately sent a telegram to the shipmaster of the Donggang, Sun Quanshun, stating, "Your telegram received. By which ship was the ship towed and to where? What is the extent of the damage? Reply in detail." After this telegram was sent, there was no reply until late at night. Until six o'clock yesterday afternoon, the Dechang Company in this city received a telegram from Cai Dachang of Fuzhou, stating that according to passengers from the Vientiane (i.e., those rescued), the Donggang's steam pipe exploded, but it did not sink. However, there are no ships to rescue it, and it is feared that it will be looted. Rescue should be expedited. (The following is omitted.) Therefore, the Donggang is still in the sea area and has not yet escaped danger. After receiving the telegram, Mr. Zhao discussed rescue measures.

▲Request for Naval Protection: Based on the telegram, the shipowner, Mr. Zhao, sent a letter to the Naval Headquarters in this city last night, requesting that a warship be dispatched to the location of the Donggang accident to protect it, in order to prevent pirate looting. On the other hand, he also discussed hiring barges to tow it for rescue and to repair the damaged areas. Yesterday, the Huaan Insurance Company, which insured the ship, sent a letter to the shipowner, inquiring about rescue measures. It is understood that the Donggang steamer has a deadweight of 1,000 tons. It originally operated in Xiangshan and was originally named Deli, but later changed to its current name. Later, as business on this route was not good, the ship was rented out to others and rerouted to Xinghua and Quanzhou, with a monthly rent of 5,500 yuan. The hull is worth 100,000 yuan, but the water insurance is not fully covered.

Yongxing Steamer Collides with Chuyou Warship

▲Negotiations for Compensation Underway

The Ningshao Company's Yongxing steamer, on the afternoon of the 18th, while traveling from Jiujiang to Hankou, collided with the Chuyou warship anchored there. The details are recorded as follows:

▲Circumstances of the Collision: The Ningshao Company's Yongxing steamer, at 8:40 p.m. on the afternoon of the 18th, set sail from Jiujiang to Hankou. Just as the ship's ropes were untied, Staff Officer Zhang of the Air Force ordered the ship to temporarily delay its departure. Therefore, it leaned against the dock again. Unexpectedly, the river water was turbulent, and the stern of the Yongxing suddenly touched a pontoon boat while untying the ropes, causing the front of the ship to be shaken and suddenly crashed into the warship Chuyou of the Navy, which was advancing on the river surface. The owner of the Yongxing ship, Wu Hougui, urgently tried to avoid it by operating the machinery, but it was too late.

▲Damage to the Warship: This collision was caused by the Yongxing steamer's starboard side striking the Chuyou warship's port side. The Chuyou was unable to avoid it due to being anchored, resulting in serious damage. At the time, the hull was about to tilt to the right. A total of one No. 3 sampan was destroyed, the warship's foremast awning support was broken, the support base was bent and damaged, the awning canvas was completely torn, the port iron chain was destroyed and broken, the medical officer's cabin on the deck was smashed, the warship's warning red light was also knocked off, the naval uniform locker was destroyed, the port water hammer disc and frame were knocked off, and the boom was also broken.

▲Joint Inspection: After the accident, the owner of the Yongxing ship, Wu Hougui, together with Mao Fengzhang, the Jiujiang branch director of Ningshao, went to the Chuyou warship and inspected it with the captain, listing all the damaged areas. Fortunately, no one was injured. Shipowner Wu expressed his apologies to the captain of the Chuyou and promised to be responsible for full compensation. After the inspection, the captain of the Chuyou dispatched his adjutant, Peng Zuxuan, to the Ningshao Company to negotiate the compensation issue.

▲Aftermath Measures: The Yongxing steamer itself also suffered considerable damage to its second-floor deck due to the huge reactive force, but it did not affect its navigation and continued to Hankou as usual. The Chuyou has reported this matter to the Naval Headquarters and is contacting Ningshao in this city to discuss repairs and compensation. The captain of the Yongxing has also reported the details of the incident to Shanghai, stating that the accident was caused by being ordered to stop sailing after already having departed. Yesterday, the company reported this matter to the General Headquarters and replied to the Naval Headquarters.

Memorial Service for Zhao Tieqiao's Death Anniversary to be Held Tomorrow

▲Simultaneously Holding a Bronze Statue Unveiling Ceremony

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Workers' Union, because tomorrow is the anniversary of the death of the late General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Zhao Tieqiao, based on the resolution of the Memorial Zhao Committee, has decided to hold it at 9:00 a.m. tomorrow (July 24th) at 7 1/2 Huangpu Beach Road. At the same time, a bronze statue unveiling ceremony for Zhao will also be held. The committee has invited people from all walks of life to participate. The memorial situation is recorded below:

▲Unveiling Ceremony: The unveiling ceremony will be performed by the current General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Guo Waifeng. The statue is one and a half feet tall, made of gold color, and was created by the artist Jiang Xiaojian. The entire project has been completed and is valued at 400 yuan. The permanent location for its placement has also been arranged by the committee with the General Management Office of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. After the memorial service, it will be moved to the Pudong Yangjiadu Riverbank to commemorate it forever.

▲Notification to Branch Offices: The committee also decided to notify all branch offices under its jurisdiction in this city and other places to fly the company flag at half-mast for one day tomorrow and to fly the flag at half-mast every year on this day thereafter to express mourning.

▲Proposals: There are also important proposals on this day, which will be submitted for discussion at the general meeting, recorded as follows: (1) Urge the National Government to expedite the public burial; (2) Commemorate the late Commissioner Zhao on July 24th every year; (3) Request the General Office to expedite the allocation of consolation money; (4) Request the court to announce the truth of the trial and pursue the main culprit.

The Matter of Leniently Admitting Female Postal Workers

▲Suspicion and Explanation

▲Petition from the Postal Workers' Union: The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, regarding the matter of leniently admitting female postal workers, submitted a document to the Ministry of Communications, stating: "Petition for instructions on leniently admitting female postal workers, requesting your consideration and instructions. Upon investigation, the Ministry's instructions to the Directorate General of Posts on June 25th stated (the text of the order was recorded in yesterday's newspaper and is omitted). Upon careful examination of the current document, it actually has a strong bias in favor of women over men, which is greatly contrary to the principle of gender equality. It is understood that the postal bureau's examination for male and female postal workers began last year. Prior to that, there were rumors that female employees would receive lower salaries and grades than men in order to save public funds. Subsequently, the union, based on the principle of gender equality, uniformly relied on examination results for recruitment and treatment, and listed practical measures regarding maternity leave and favorable regulations for female transfers, and suggested that the Directorate General of Posts submit them to the Ministry for approval and implementation. This fully demonstrates the union's sincere respect for the spirit of gender equality, its efforts to seek welfare for female colleagues, its efforts to eliminate gender barriers in society, and its efforts to resolve disputes over gender divisions in the postal service. I am pleased that the new system has just been implemented and the grand plan is gradually unfolding. Unexpectedly, this time, the recruitment of postal workers in Shanghai, Fujian, and other regions suddenly favors women over men. Is this in accordance with party guidelines? Examinations should naturally not be divided by gender and should take academic knowledge as the standard. How can one favor this and discriminate against that, going against the principle of equality? Upon careful examination of the order, it first states that there are many women with higher education, and then it states that women should be leniently admitted. The postal bureau's examination has always been based on selecting true talent. This is not only something that postal colleagues are confident in, but also something that the whole country agrees with. If the women who take the examination do have higher education, it will naturally be easy to be selected. Why is it necessary to be leniently admitted? Furthermore, various agencies have never had abnormal regulations for preferential recruitment of female employees. The Ministry has created this example, which those who know it will say is promoting women's employment, and those who criticize it will say is belittling women. It is truly something that the Ministry does not approve of. The union members are greatly puzzled, so they have submitted a special petition, requesting your consideration and a detailed explanation of the instructions for compliance, in order to dispel the doubts of the people. This is truly for the public convenience. Respectfully submitted to the Minister of Communications, Wang, respectfully submitted by the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, July 23rd."

▲Secretary Yang's Remarks: A reporter from the Daily News inquired about this matter with Secretary Yang Ketian of the bureau yesterday. According to him, the wording of the order received from the Ministry of Communications this time seemed quite vague. The only thing that favors women is the statement that female candidates should be leniently admitted to show encouragement. However, in my (Yang's self-designation) opinion, the so-called lenient treatment of women actually means leniently admitting them in terms of physical examination. Because women are inherently insufficient, their physical strength is not as good as men's. Therefore, there is this order to make up for women's shortcomings. Judging by the principle of equality, there seems to be nothing wrong with it. As for academic knowledge in the examination, men and women are still equal and there is no division. I have heard that the Postal Workers' Union opposes this, saying that it does not conform to gender equality. I have always advocated recruiting more women to show the promotion of women's rights. This time, I thought that the so-called lenient admission in the Ministry of Communications' order was in terms of academic knowledge, so I expressed dissatisfaction. If I knew that this time the leniency was in terms of physical fitness and that the standard for academic knowledge in the examination was still equality, I think I would not object to it.

Shipping Companies Request Exemption from Deck Tonnage Dues

▲The Shipping Association Submitted a Document to the Ministry of Finance Yesterday

The Shanghai Shipping Association submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance, stating: "Petition for the additional levy of tonnage dues on goods loaded on decks, etc., which is of absolutely no benefit to preventing smuggling and ensuring security, and is cumbersome and repetitive, making it unbearable. We respectfully reiterate the facts and implore you to quickly withdraw your order, so as to avoid double taxation and maintain commercial shipping. Your association previously submitted a request to exempt the additional levy of tonnage dues on goods loaded on decks, etc., and received your approval, stating that the submission was noted. The additional levy of tonnage dues on goods loaded on decks was originally for the purpose of preventing smuggling and ensuring security, and was implemented with the approval of the Executive Yuan, making it difficult to change. If there are other difficulties, the association may directly negotiate with the customs on methods to facilitate shipping companies, while still adhering to the purpose of not violating the Executive Yuan's order, which should be complied with. Upon investigation, ships have a wider space, and it is difficult to avoid goods being carried without declaration by cargo vendors, crew members, and their subordinates. However, since it is smuggling, it is inevitable that the customs officers will search, the captains will investigate, and the inspectors will investigate. The goods are hidden and concealed. Even the most foolish person would never publicly place smuggled goods on the visible decks, etc., to await discovery. Therefore, the method of preventing smuggling by adding tonnage dues on goods loaded on decks, etc., is actually prescribing the wrong medicine and is ridiculed by smugglers. This is the first point. Upon investigation, the goods loaded on decks, etc., are either poultry, fish, fruits, vegetables, etc., which are related to death, rot, and collapse, or cotton, rags, oil, etc., which are related to fire hazards and abandonment, or empty joints, empty cages, empty barrels, etc., which are related to avoiding pressure and facilitating unloading. All of these have special reasons why they cannot be loaded in cargo holds. Furthermore, the above-mentioned items occupy more space and weigh less, so loading on decks, etc., will never cause the upper part to be heavy and the lower part to be light, endangering safety. Even if encountering wind and waves along the way, they can be thrown into the sea immediately. The jettisoning of deck cargo is permitted by cargo passengers and is a common practice in the shipping industry. According to the shipping regulations of various countries, such goods are also excluded from general average. From this perspective, it has absolutely no impact on navigation safety. If it is said that adding tonnage dues on decks is intended to prohibit through taxation, so that goods loaded on decks, etc., will be moved to cargo holds in the future, the reasons are special and it is impossible to do so in reality. Therefore, this measure is also inconsistent with the topic and cannot achieve any results. This is the second point. Upon investigation, after the tonnage of each ship is determined by the customs, in order to prevent shipowners from greedily loading too much, a mark of the load line (commonly known as the insurance circle) is added on both sides of the ship's outer surface to indicate the limit. In this regard, the weight of each cargo that should be exposed on decks, etc., is actually included in the ship's rated tonnage. Since it is included in the rated tonnage, the tonnage dues have already been paid, and demanding additional payment is called double taxation. If the weight of the entire ship exceeds the load line due to the installation of cargo on decks, etc., then its export should be absolutely prohibited in order to rectify it and ensure safety. It is absolutely not allowed to voluntarily pay additional tonnage dues to be granted a violation. Otherwise, if the ship is within the limit of its load capacity, it will be required to pay additional tonnage dues per ton and per trip solely because of the different location of the cargo. This is seeking an exception outside the law. What's more, if each ship's cargo is insufficient for its rated tonnage each time, I know that the customs will definitely not agree to return the tonnage dues for the unused tonnage of cargo this time. If so, the method of receiving and giving is different. In terms of emotion, reason, affairs, and law, it is difficult to justify itself. This is the third point. To the extent that smuggling is enough to damage the income of shipowners, shipowners are doing everything they can to prevent it in order to protect their income. Therefore, they all hire many inspectors to detect or intercept on ships or in ports. Before departure and upon arrival of the ship, customs officers conduct searches, confiscate, and punish. Nothing is omitted. This is all the proper way to prevent smuggling, and it is what wealthy merchants are doing in practice. If the customs wants to seek a progressive method in order to stop smuggling, it can formulate a method that prescribes the right medicine. All shipowners will sincerely welcome and fully assist. Otherwise, this additional levy of tonnage dues on goods loaded on decks, etc., is of no benefit to preventing smuggling, is irrelevant to ensuring safety, and is a type of double taxation if the cargo is not over-limit. It is truly impossible for the shipping companies, which are extremely depressed, to reluctantly assume. In addition to complying with the approval to recommend representatives to meet with the Jianghai Customs Tax Affairs Department to discuss everything and request him to forward it, we respectfully reiterate the facts and implore you to carefully examine them and quickly withdraw your order, so as to avoid double taxation and maintain commercial shipping. We urgently present our words and await your orders in fear. Respectfully presented to the Ministry of Finance. The letter to the Tax Affairs Department is roughly the same and is omitted."

The Daji Steamer Will Resume Service

▲Renamed Dayu

The Dada Company's Shanghai-Yangtze River route steamer Daji, which exploded with sulfur on the Longjusha River off the coast of Tianshenggang on the evening of March 11, burning hundreds of people to death and completely destroying the ship's surface, etc., was reported in detail in previous newspapers. The hull of the ship was later retrieved to Shanghai by the company and repaired at the Ruirong Shipyard in Yangshupu. After more than four months, it is now heard that the ship's renovation is about to be completed and it will leave the factory in early next month, resuming service around mid-month. The former name of Daji has now been changed to Dayu. It is heard that the Daji steamer's losses this time are over 200,000.

The Shanghai Industrial Survey Extension Ends

The Shanghai Industrial Survey, conducted by the State Council's Directorate General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics, the Ministry of Industry, the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, and other five agencies, has been underway since May, with a period of three months until the end of this month. A total of 1,700 large and small factories have been surveyed. However, there are approximately 2,000 domestic factories in Shanghai, and there may still be omissions. Furthermore, the forms filled out by each factory often have conflicting figures, which will inevitably cause difficulties in compiling statistics in the future. Therefore, after reviewing the forms, about half of them still need to be reviewed and corrected before they can be compiled. Yesterday, representatives from various agencies held a meeting and decided to extend the aforementioned supplementary investigation and review period by another three months, which will not be completed until the end of October this year. However, there were previously sixteen investigators, and it is now proposed to reduce them by half.

News of Concessions in the City Center Yesterday

▲The Spirit of Service of the Shanghai Bank

The day before yesterday (21st) was the first time the municipal government started to allow citizens to purchase land in the city center. Because the location is suitable and prosperity is expected, the leaders were very crowded, so the district time was specially changed to a lottery method. As a result of the lottery, the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank obtained more than twenty districts. However, it is heard that many people had entrusted the bank to bid on their behalf in advance. Therefore, as a result, in addition to each trustee obtaining a certain number of acres (approximately 40% of the total), everyone felt that they had not fully satisfied their wishes. The bank itself only obtained 40 acres. It is also heard that the bank's role in obtaining land is, on the one hand, to promote the prosperity of the city center, and on the other hand, to solve the housing difficulties of citizens. Therefore, it plans to build beautiful houses for sale on the land it has obtained, with separate deeds for each house, and the purchase price can be repaid in installments, and the price is also low. It is absolutely not for profit. However, the land currently obtained is limited and can only meet the needs of the bank's employees. Therefore, the bank authorities are willing to provide assistance with construction funds to anyone from any sector who has obtained the land in the same spirit. It is heard that they are currently drafting measures for construction loans.

The Barges in the Chongxin Cotton Mill Have Been Resolved

The Shanghai Customs Brokerage Industry Union, due to the new wooden bridge built in front of the Chongxin Cotton Mill in Huxi, canceled the barges used since July 1st. When customs brokerage workers went to pick up the goods, they had to be transported by self-employed porters, which was quite inconvenient. They flocked to the union to report the matter and requested the restoration of the original barges. The union sent people to negotiate, but the negotiations broke down, resulting in a dispute. Later, the union sent a letter to the Cotton Yarn Industry Market, instructing the factory to restore the barges. Yesterday, a reply was received from the Cotton Yarn Market, informing that the factory had agreed to restore the original barges. The dispute has therefore come to an end.

Local News 2

Sudden Cool Weather's Impact

▲Sudden Coolness… Breeding Numerous Diseases

▲Rainfall… Reports of Disaster from Various Villages

We are in the Great Heat period, but the weather has drastically changed. For the past few days, it was unusually sweltering, but for the last two days, it has suddenly become extremely cool. The Fahrenheit thermometer has plummeted to 73 degrees. A cool breeze is blowing, and there is continuous rain. Wearing only thin cloth clothes is not enough to keep warm. Older people are all wearing lined clothes and need to cover themselves with thin blankets and padded mattresses at night. This weather is like that of the fifth month. Compared to the scorching heat of last week, there is a difference of about 30 degrees. The impact on various aspects is recorded below:

▲Widespread Human Illnesses: Since the continuous rain and alternating warm and cold weather in this city, there have been outbreaks of epidemics in various places. In the last two days, it has suddenly become too cool, and people are experiencing fever and headaches. In severe cases, there is incessant vomiting. As a result, the number of patients seeking treatment at the epidemic hospitals in this city has suddenly increased, and the hospital wards are overflowing with patients. This is mostly due to catching a cold. If one is careless and does not cover themselves with a thin blanket at night, illness will immediately occur. We hope that everyone will pay extra attention.

▲Losses for Cold Drink Vendors: During the hot season, cold drink shops on various roads in this city were originally thriving. However, the recent cool weather, with no sweat on people's bodies, naturally leads to a lack of customers for ice cream, shaved ice, soda, and other cold products. It is also reported that the first batches of watermelons and cantaloupes purchased by fruit businesses in both the northern and southern markets are unsellable. Although the price is only about three yuan per load, the cold weather means there are few buyers. Therefore, businesses are greatly affected. Fortunately, the goods are still fresh, and the losses are limited.

▲Repeated Reports of Floods in Various Villages: Since the torrential rain on the 6th of this month, it has been half a month of continuous rain, causing rivers to swell. As a result, low-lying areas in Pudong and western Shanghai have become a vast expanse of water. Rice paddies and vegetables are submerged. Farmers are anxiously hoping for sunny weather and receding water so they can salvage their crops. Unexpectedly, it continues to rain, and the water level is rising drastically in secret. Flood conditions are already apparent. According to people from Jiangsu and Zhejiang, farmland in various villages such as Dongting Mountain, Mudu, Tangkou, and Hongta in Suzhou has been submerged. Rice seedlings are floating on the water. Farmers are rushing to the county to report crop failures, almost continuously on the road. It is also reported that Shaoxing and Wenzhou in Zhejiang have also become watery regions. In addition, mountain torrents have erupted, creating a severe situation. The people are suffering great losses, and disaster conditions are in place. There is a fear of a complete loss of the autumn harvest.

Husband is Congenitally Impotent, Wife Sues for Divorce

▲No Conjugal Relations for Over a Year

▲Plaintiff is Still a Virgin

▲Husband and Mother-in-Law Frequently Abuse Her

▲Seeking Compensation and Divorce

Li Tangshi, a woman from Jiangbei, 21 years old, married Li Shengfang from Ningbo last March. Now she has hired lawyer Gao Wenqi to file a lawsuit in the special court, requesting permission to divorce and demanding that Li Shengfang pay a total of 2,900 yuan in consolation and living expenses. The reason is that Li suffers from congenital impotence. After more than a year of marriage, they have never had conjugal relations, and he has abused her. Her complaint states: The plaintiff married Li Shengfang last March through matchmaker Zhang Jinsheng. Unexpectedly, the defendant suffers from a hidden disease and cannot engage in sexual relations. Therefore, for more than a year, the plaintiff has remained a virgin. Both parties can be examined to verify this. They are husband and wife in name only, with no emotional connection. The greatest desire of life is completely extinguished (commonly known as "congenital impotence," which is what is referred to in item 7 of Article 1052 of the Family Law as "having an incurable, serious disease"). The plaintiff's mother-in-law and husband do not treat her with the respect due a daughter-in-law but treat her like a servant. If she disagrees with them, she is abused, and the abuse gradually increases to physical assault. On the ninth day of the first lunar month of this year, she was beaten with bamboo sticks and tied with hemp ropes, resulting in injuries all over her body. Her mother-in-law aided and abetted the abuse. The matter was reported to the police station. On March 28 of this year, due to a trivial matter, the defendant pressed the plaintiff's face onto broken glass, causing serious facial injuries and profuse bleeding. She went to the Shanghai South People's Hospital for treatment and obtained a medical certificate. She also filed a self-accusation of assault in the criminal court of your court, but it was rejected because it did not meet the self-accusation regulations. However, the defendant, suffering from a serious illness, should not have married the plaintiff, causing her lifelong harm. Furthermore, this behavior clearly constitutes malicious abandonment. Her lifelong happiness has been stripped away by him. Given the marital facts, it is impossible to live together. Therefore, according to the provisions of Article 1056 of the Family Law, the defendant should compensate her for the loss of 500 yuan in order to console her for the harm and abandonment, leaving her unable to support herself. The defendant should pay living expenses of at least 20 yuan per month, which, calculated over ten years, amounts to 2,400 yuan. Furthermore, based on the precedents of the Supreme Court's judgments Shang Zi No. 1457 in the fifth year, No. 1073, No. 634 in the sixth year, and the second clause of the resolution on the women's movement of the Second National Congress of the National Government, it is requested that the plaintiff be granted a divorce from the defendant Li Shengfang. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong opened the court to summon and question them. Li Tangshi stated the facts of the case, but the defendant stated in his defense: "I used to work in a foreign goods shop opened by my cousin, Shi Zhenmin. Now that Shi's shop has closed down, I have returned to my hometown. I have no residence in Shanghai and am only temporarily living at my cousin's house." He also hired a lawyer to raise the issue of jurisdiction. Judge Xu verified the statements and stated that the case still needs investigation and will be questioned after clarification.

Zou Aizhen Sues Dr. Tang for Divorce

▲Demands 10,000 Yuan in Alimony

▲Demands 10,000 Yuan for Children's Education

The lawsuit between Dr. Tang Huixuan (i.e., Tang Chongci), an economics PhD, and his wife Zou Aizhen in the Shanghai District Court has been ongoing for nearly ten months. The newspapers have reported it countless times. Now Tang Huixuan has filed another lawsuit in the Special District Court, which is still in progress. Zou Aizhen, on the other hand, has hired lawyer Yang Zhihao to apply for divorce in the mediation court of the District Court. Because the defendant did not appear, the mediation failed. Zou then formally filed a lawsuit for divorce, demanding 10,000 yuan in alimony and 10,000 yuan for her children's education expenses. She also requested assistance with the litigation costs. Her statement roughly stated that the defendant, Tang Chongci, had abandoned her and that she was requesting a judgment to order him to pay alimony and grant the divorce. The plaintiff married the defendant, Tang Chongci, i.e., Tang Huixuan, in 1923. Not long after the marriage, she discovered that the defendant already had a wife in his hometown of Guangxi. She negotiated with him, and the defendant wrote a letter of repentance, which was kept as evidence. At that time, the plaintiff and defendant were in a foreign land, and the plaintiff was helpless and unable to resist, so she endured the humiliation and sought peace, hoping for eternal love and happiness. After returning to China, the defendant could not find a job and was in difficult circumstances. The plaintiff used her mother's savings to help him, and even mortgaged her mother's family property to support him. He then obtained the position of director of the Yichang stamp tax bureau. At the beginning of his tenure, the plaintiff did not go with him. Later, she heard that he was spending lavishly in Yichang, gambling and engaging in prostitution. The plaintiff, fearing that he would run out of money and his reputation would be ruined, which would affect his job, went to Yichang to advise him. Unexpectedly, the defendant was overly enthusiastic at the time, and her honest advice fell on deaf ears, which angered him and caused a rift. Not long after, the defendant was dismissed. Afterward, disagreements arose, and their relationship deteriorated. She still remembers the tragic events of the night before August 18 last year. The defendant had a secret rendezvous with a woman who had come from Guangdong in a hotel. When the defendant first returned, the plaintiff immediately noticed that his actions were strange and secretly monitored him. That is why she went to confront him in person, resulting in an unhappy breakup. The defendant then conspired to launch a preemptive strike, intending to trap the plaintiff in a perpetual state of misery. Fortunately, your court saw through his plan, and her grievances were redressed. However, the defendant used this as an excuse to shirk his responsibilities, completely disregarding the plaintiff and her children. How can this be justified? The love between husband and wife has already broken down, but without a legal divorce, the defendant's crime of abandonment cannot be denied. The plaintiff is struggling to survive and raise her children and cannot bear it any longer. She requests permission for a divorce and alimony, etc. At 10:00 a.m. on the morning of the hearing, Judge Tong Shenglv opened the eighth court to hear the case. The defendant, Tang Chongci, did not appear. Only the plaintiff, accompanied by lawyer Yang Zhihao, appeared in court. Zou Aizhen testified that she was 26 years old, a native of Shanghai, and currently residing at No. 20 Wenmiao Road. She also recounted the previous events, stating that on August 16 last year, the defendant's companion first dragged out her younger sister, realizing that it was a mistake, and then dragged her out, falsely accusing her of improper behavior. His sinister intentions are evident. The judge said, "Your request for divorce is falling into the defendant's trap." She replied, "Previously, the defendant wanted me to divorce him privately, promising to give me 2,000 yuan. Because I have not committed any wrongdoing, I refused. Now that the defendant has such intentions, I fear being framed again if we reconcile." The judge said, "The defendant is not present today. We will summon him again for review." The court was then adjourned.

However, they all feel that transportation by boat and car, as well as food and accommodation, are inconvenient. Therefore, the Putuo Tour Service Society has been established this summer. Public Memorial for Hardoon

▲The Tablet Was Inscribed the Day Before Yesterday, the Memorial Service is Held Today

▲A Sea of White in Aili Garden

After the death of the Jewish tycoon Hardoon, the Aili Garden funeral committee arranged for the inscription of the memorial tablet and the distribution of obituaries. The inscription ceremony was held on the 21st, and yesterday was the family memorial service and public memorial service. The funeral will begin today. Two white memorial arches were erected in front of the Aili Garden gate. The garden was a sea of white. Funeral couplets and memorial banners were hung everywhere, totaling no less than tens of thousands. From the 21st, Zhang Enpu, the 63rd generation Heavenly Master of Longhu Mountain, was invited to set up a Taoist altar for three days. Dozens of lamas from the Yonghe Temple in Beijing were also chanting sutras. The ceremonies were extremely grand. During the inscription of the tablet, Liu Chunlin, the former Qing Dynasty's Zhuangyuan (top scholar) from Tianjin, was specially invited to Shanghai to inscribe the tablet. Xia Shoutian, the former Qing Dynasty's Bangyan (second-place scholar), and Zheng Yuan, the Tanhua (third-place scholar), served as assistant officials. The ceremony followed ancient traditions. Yesterday's public memorial service program was as follows: (1) Alumni Association of the Cang Sheng Ming Zhi University; (2) Aili Garden Staff; (3) Employees of Hardoon Foreign Company; (4) Foremen of various construction projects; (5) Tenants from various roads; (6) Students; (7) Xuzhou Fellow Villagers Association; (8) Forty-four charitable organizations in this city, such as the Poor Children's Home, Women's Reformatory, Tongren Fuyuan Hall, Zhepu Yutang, China Jisheng Association, Shanghai Disabled People's Hospital, and Qiliu Public Institute, etc. From 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m., mourners came continuously, filling the streets with plain carriages and white horses, a display of extreme grief for the time.

Pudong Electric Company Implements Loan Program for Installing Lights

丨Effective August 1st of this Year丨

▲Facilitating Citizens and Developing Businesses

▲Other Electric Companies Can Follow Suit

For the past year, due to the high price of gold and the low price of silver, kerosene prices have continued to rise. Considering the situation of the general public, it is more convenient and economical to use electric lights than to burn kerosene lamps. However, the cost of installing lights is quite high, so some people are temporarily limited by their financial resources and delay the installation. The Pudong Electric Company, in order to help common households popularize electricity, has specially formulated a loan program for installing lights, as follows: (1) Registration: Anyone who wants to install electric lights but cannot pay the installation fee in full and wants to borrow money from the company to repay it in installments can go to the company (at the Zhangjiabangkou in Pudong) or registered electrical shops or electrical installers (hereinafter referred to as installers) to fill out a "Loan Application for Installing Lights" and find a reliable guarantor to co-sign and seal it and submit it to the company. After investigation and approval, they will be registered, and a "Loan Registration Form for Installing Lights" along with a blank loan certificate will be mailed to the household to be effective. (2) Number of Households: Starting from August 1, 1931, the program is limited to 1,000 households and will be terminated when the quota is full. If the quota is not full by December 31, it will not be extended. (3) Type of Households: Limited to new households that have not yet installed lights. Households that have already installed lights and want to add more lights are not eligible. (4) Location: Limited to areas covered by the company's current power lines. It does not include areas where additional poles and lines are required to connect to electricity. (5) Number of Lights: This program is specifically designed to help small households, so each household is limited to three to five lights. Loan will not be given to those who need to install six or more lights. (6) Guarantee: Limited to shops near the household that have already installed electric lights and have not borrowed money from the company under this program to install lights. The company may add restrictions if the number of guaranteed households is too large. (7) Installation Fee: The installation fee and wire costs are determined by the household and the installer. The company is not involved. However, if the installer charges excessive fees or demands extra expenses, it can be reported to the company for investigation. (8) Loan: For each light installed, the company can borrow three yuan and five jiao without interest. Upon completion of the installation, the loan certificate must be filled out in the prescribed form, co-signed and sealed by the guarantor, and brought to the company with the installer to receive the loan. The installation fee and wire costs will be settled with the installer on the spot and paid in full. If the expenses exceed the loan amount, the household must pay the difference. (9) Repayment: The loan is repaid in twelve monthly installments, with each light costing three jiao per month. After full repayment, the light line will be fully owned by the household. If payment is not made on time, the guarantor is responsible for handling it. An additional one jiao per light will be charged to compensate the company for the cost of printing documents and affixing stamp duties. (10) Deposit: The deposit for installing lights must still be paid in full at the time of application, according to the company's business regulations. (11) Supplementary Provisions: In addition to the items listed in this program, other matters not covered will be handled in accordance with the company's business regulations. It is reported that the Municipal Public Works Bureau believes that this program can facilitate citizens in installing lights and develop the company's business, achieving both goals. In addition to approving its filing, it has also ordered other electric companies in the city to follow suit when necessary.

Further Investigation into the Murder of Ou Zhenbang: Suspect Li Rudian Apprehended

Ou Zhenbang, a native of Guangdong, was beaten to death in front of the Guang Wu Tai Theater on Qiujiang Road in Zhabei at around 2:00 a.m. on the 1st of this month. Subsequently, the Public Security Bureau arrested Huo Dongsheng, a native of Guangdong, as the perpetrator. Under interrogation, he implicated Li Rudian, a Guangdong native residing at No. 694 North Sichuan Road. The day before yesterday, Li was arrested by Chen Keqing, a detective from the Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, together with Liang Yongji, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Special District Court. Judge Feng Shide conducted a preliminary hearing. In addition to submitting official documents requesting extradition, Detective Chen brought Huo Dongsheng to testify in the case. Because the thugs were overwhelming, he immediately fled. The next day, he heard that Ou had been killed. Worker Killed in Machine Accident

Xu Handing, a 23-year-old native of Shaoxing Yuyao and a worker in the machine shop of the Xiangtai Timber Company at No. 80 Yangshupu Road, was repairing a machine in the machine shop at 11:10 p.m. the night before last. Due to a moment of carelessness, he was caught in the machine's belt. Xu immediately passed out. His colleague Ye Zonglong noticed this and quickly turned off the machine's power. He then tried to rescue him, but Xu had suffered severe injuries, and his left leg had been crushed. He reported the incident to the Yangshupu Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. Xu was taken to the Tongren Hospital, but due to the severity of his injuries, he died shortly after. His body was sent to the forensic institute on Fielun Road. Yesterday morning, Guo Huaipu, a prosecutor from the Special District Court, visited the institute for an autopsy. He took statements, and the witness Ye Zonglong reported the details of the incident. Subsequently, the deceased's wife, Shen, filed a complaint, stating that the deceased was her husband, she had come to Shanghai from her hometown not long ago, and there were still her mother-in-law and children at home. The family of several people all depended on her husband for support. Now that he had died tragically, she requested that the court order the timber company to provide generous compensation. After verifying the statements, Judge Guo declared that Xu Handing, the deceased, had indeed been working for the Xiangtai Timber Company and had been crushed to death by the machine. The body was handed over to his wife, Xu Shenshi, to arrange for the funeral.

Pigtails Cause a lot of harm

▲The end of the pigtail was brought into the locomotive, causing brain injury

▲Eyes and ears bleeding, still in a dangerous period

Tang Mou's daughter, named Nannan, a 14-year-old resident of Chuanhong Port, Pudong, across the Wusong River, was a helper in the fine yarn room of the Huafeng Yarn Factory. When she was leaving the factory at 5:00 a.m. yesterday, a female co-worker named Yin A'mei, a 17-year-old native of Sitangqiao, Songbei, asked Nannan to comb her hair. Nannan, not wanting to refuse out of politeness, combed Yin's pigtail for her. In her confusion, she accidentally brought the end of her own pigtail into the locomotive, and her head was pulled in. She was immediately rescued by others, and the driver stopped the car immediately. Because the back of her head was severely injured, causing her eyes and ears to bleed non-stop, she immediately lost consciousness. Later, she was sent to the Wusong Seaside Public Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor at the hospital, because her head had been subjected to severe trauma, causing damage to her brain, she would only be out of danger if there were no changes within three days. Currently, Nannan's parents have filed a complaint with Yin A'mei's parents.

A Record of the Public Changlong Sandboat's Disaster

▲First hit by a hurricane, then by pirates

▲Crew Member Wu Bochen and the Ship Owner Sigh in Despair

The Public Changlong sandboat, owned by the Public Profit Company, used to sail to Southeast Asia, carrying passengers and cargo. This spring, because there were not many passengers and cargo going from Shanghai, it changed its route to North China, including Yingkou, Andong, and Dalian, to transport goods for sale. The company specifically set up branches in Yingkou and Andong. The ship loaded with native cloth and woollen goods, etc. from Shanghai at the beginning of last month, and transported them to Andong to unload and sell, for more than 40,000 taels of silver, which was used to purchase soybean oil and goods from the north. It was loaded onto the ship on the 5th of this month to return to Shanghai. Unexpectedly, when it reached the waters off Tongshan, a hurricane suddenly erupted, and the waves were fierce and urgent, crashing onto the deck. Four crew members working on deck were washed away by the waves. The ship owner was frightened and, seeing that there was no port nearby to seek shelter, instructed the helmsman to turn the rudder and head straight for the coast. Unexpectedly, the wind and waves became even more violent. Just as he was turning the rudder, the rudder was smashed by a huge wave, causing it to lose steering power. The crew was helpless and had to retreat to the cabin. Then, a huge wave crashed the ship onto the outer beach of Chongming, hitting the front half of the ship. The ship broke and ran aground on the sand. The crew, seeing that it was not far from Wusong, planned to send a boat to Shanghai to report. They sent a boat to unload the goods. Suddenly, the pirates learned of this. At midnight, they arrived in several ships and robbed the goods from the north. The soybean oil jars were broken, and the oil leaked out. The pirates, seeing that the jars were empty, were furious and threw them into the sea. Yesterday, the Public Profit Company received the report. The value of the ship and cargo was estimated at 120,000-130,000 taels. It is said that the bottom of the ship was broken by ten feet and could not be repaired. A steamer has now been hired to transport the crew, tools, and other items back to Shanghai. The ship itself is to be sold. A reward has been offered for the four crew members washed away, and fishing boats in the Tongshan area have been entrusted to search for their bodies.

Despondent Youth Jumps into the Huangpu River, Rescued

At 11:00 p.m. the night before last, a young man boarded a sampan and jumped into the Huangpu River at the mouth of the Suzhou River to commit suicide. Fortunately, he was rescued by the sampan operator, who reported it to Chinese Constable No. 14 of the Customs Water Patrol. The constable took him to the police station. He identified himself as Zhang Zihua, 20 years old, from Yunnan, residing at No. 35 Jufuxi Fang. He had no job in Shanghai and planned to go to Xuzhou to find a friend to seek employment, but he had no travel expenses. Therefore, he pawned a long gown for only eight jiao, which was not enough to cover his travel expenses. While on the tram, a pickpocket stole all eight jiao. After discovering it, the thief had already fled far away. Thinking that his fate was hopeless, he decided to commit suicide by jumping into the Huangpu River to avoid starving to death. Fourteen copper coins, ten pawn tickets, and a few miscellaneous items were found on his person. When asked if he had any relatives in Shanghai, he said that he had an uncle named Zhang Zhongliang. The head constable dispatched Detective Huang Songsheng to inform his uncle, who sent someone to the police station to take Zhang back.

National Physicians' Association Requests French Concession to Exempt Doctors from Levies

The Shanghai National Physicians' Association, regarding the French Concession's collection of levies from doctors, sent a letter to the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association, stating: "We respectfully write to inform you that previously, when the French Municipal Council (FMC) organized the registration of doctors, our association and the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau negotiated with the FMC. We were granted permission for a one-time registration, with a fee of two yuan. Doctors from outside the Concession were not required to register. This was confirmed in a written reply to our association. Now, according to reports from our members, the FMC, in addition to the registration, is levying a 'health donation,' requiring each doctor to pay two yuan annually. Although the amount is small, it contradicts the FMC's letter to our association dated February 27th, which stated that the registration fee was a one-time charge. Furthermore, doctors are a type of free profession, similar in nature to lawyers and accountants. It is difficult to categorize them as being in the same category as restaurants, thereby subjecting them to a health bureau levy and requiring annual payments. Moreover, other Chinese concessions and settlements do not have precedents for requiring doctors to pay levies. Forcing them to pay levies not only causes unnecessary disturbances, but the total amount collected would also be less than a thousand yuan, which the bureau should not collect. We believe your association is a taxpayers' organization in the French Concession and the voice of the Chinese people. We request that you forward a letter to the FMC to exempt doctors from the health donation. We earnestly hope for this. Respectfully submitted to the French Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association by the Shanghai National Physicians' Association."

Tongzhou Channel Buoy About to Be Moved

The Customs Maritime Affairs Section Patrol Engineering Office (No. 1008) announces: It has been instructed by the River and Sea Customs Tax Department that the Tongzhou Channel buoy within its jurisdiction is about to be moved. The situation and position are listed below: The Yangtze River Tongzhou Channel buoy will be moved around July 23rd. The new location is thirty-one and a half degrees east of south from the Xu Liujing Mouth pile (according to compass direction), at a distance of three and seventy-one hundredths English nautical miles. The other conditions remain the same. Refer to Chinese Navy Hydrographic Chart No. 142 for clarity. This announcement must be followed, and all ships must pay close attention and record the details to avoid negligence. Patrol Engineering Officer Xi Liman, July 17th, Republic of China Year 20.

Lianmei to Perform at Penglai Theater Tomorrow

The Lianmei Dance Troupe, led by Wei Yingbo with more than fifty members, which once performed at the Shanghai Summer Pick and Central New Central theaters, and went to Nanjing, Suzhou, and Wuxi for public performances, returned to Shanghai yesterday. It immediately accepted an invitation from the Penglai Theater in this city and is scheduled to perform for the second time in Shanghai starting tomorrow.

Theaters Re-releasing Ji Gong the Living Buddha

"Ji Gong the Living Buddha," produced by the former Kaixin Film Company, is one of the most famous works in Chinese-made slapstick films. At the time, it was very popular in various places. After Kaixin reorganized, the film disappeared. It is now reported that starting tomorrow, the entire first, second, third, and fourth episodes will be screened at the Wanguo Theater in Hongkou, with two episodes being screened every three days, completed in two phases. The Cade, Zhonghua, Empire, World, and other theaters will also be screening it in succession.

News from Trade Associations

▲ Freight Trucking Industry The Freight Trucking Industry Association, regarding the tragic anti-Chinese incident by Koreans, convened its fifth executive committee meeting yesterday (the 20th) to discuss everything. Chairman Jiang Zhongying. Matters discussed: (1) All sectors of Shanghai have established anti-Japanese and overseas Chinese aid associations for the anti-Chinese incident by Koreans. This association should also express its sympathy. All members of this association will no longer transport Japanese goods from today to show their indignation. All members unanimously approved this, and the association will send a letter to all members to comply. (2) The Tax Regulations Research Association requested the purchase of operating guidelines. Should they be printed? It was decided to print two hundred copies. (3) From the previous resolution, how many permanent legal advisors should be hired? It was decided to hire two lawyers as permanent legal advisors to the association. (4) The association's affairs are very busy. Should a design committee be added? It was decided to start organizing immediately, with a maximum of seven members.

Then, permanent committee members and representatives to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce were elected. Yu Mingxun was nominated as the external representative to first go to the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Chinese Aid Association to liaise with various sectors. Internally, all members will be notified to boycott Japanese goods from today onwards, in accordance with the resolutions of the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Chinese Aid Association. On the 25th of this month, a meeting of Chinese electrical appliance factories will be convened to consult on the total output of Chinese factories to facilitate budgeting and to plan for a fundamental and permanent boycott.

▲ Cigar Industry There are about twenty or thirty cigar factories in Shanghai. They once organized an association, but the registration procedures were not completed, resulting in failure. Now, due to the current situation, the industry believes that it is necessary to establish a trade association for protection and to maintain the market. Ten or more people, including Teng Zhixiang, Shen Rongxuan, and He Shenji, initiated the reorganization of the original association and applied for registration. It has taken more than two months since preparations began. The Municipal Party Department's Civil Training Committee issued approval No. 4184 the day before, approving the establishment and issuing a certificate. The association received the certificate and immediately issued a notice of assembly, scheduling an important meeting today to arrange the steps to be taken.

News from Various Native Place Associations

▲ Ningbo According to reports to the Ningbo Native Place Association, a Ningbo woman, Mrs. Chen Ni, lives on Route Ghisi, in poor circumstances, and earns a living by washing clothes. The day before, a customer entrusted her with washing a bed sheet. When it was sent back, it was mixed up with another customer's. The customer demanded the original item. Mrs. Chen admitted that if the original bed sheet could not be found, she would compensate accordingly. The customer stated that if the original item could not be found, compensation of more than ten yuan would be required, which led to a dispute. The customer then invited companions to Mrs. Chen's home to cause trouble. Neighbors intervened to persuade them to leave. After hearing the news, the association sent a letter to the Caojiadu Public Security Sub-bureau, asking them to investigate.

▲ First District Transport Workers' Union The Sand and Gravel Office held its fifth meeting of cadres the day before. Chairman Tao Benrong. It was reported that the excavation and transportation of floating sand from Xiaoxikou, Zhejiang, has been going on for many years. Traditionally, each boat owner bears the burden of contributing to the local primary school, which is five cents per ton. This is already a heavy burden. Unexpectedly, this year, the contractor contracted to collect the local school contribution, falsely collecting sand and mud, at a cost of 20-30 cents per ton. As the government considers the people's difficulties and implements the abolition of taxes, they are falsely collecting donations. It is justified to request the government to thoroughly investigate and abolish this, to alleviate the people's hardship. Representatives have been sent to the Zhejiang Provincial authorities to petition. (B) Discussion (1) All members of the association who mine floating sand from Xiaoxikou should only pay the local school donation of five cents per ton, and no other burden should be borne. (2) The members of the association should be reorganized. The association does not protect non-members. If members are found to have not paid membership fees for several months, they should be warned to pay them as soon as possible. (3) Collect a temporary special donation from each member and submit a document to the superior agency for record. (4) Issue membership cards for identification. All of the above proposals were passed by the meeting and adjourned.

Letter to the Editor

Dear Editor, I recently read the news article "Stepmother Abuses Daughter to Death Case" published in your newspaper on the 19th of this month. The content has some discrepancies. I would like to inform you as follows: My late wife, Mrs. He, passed away from illness only half a month after giving birth to my daughter, Bao Yun. At that time, there was no one to breastfeed her. Every possible nurturing method was used to ensure her survival, which I was very happy about. After five years, due to the lack of a wife, it was inconvenient, so I remarried. Her stepmother loved her very much, and her grandparents also loved her very much. She was able to reach the age of sixteen, and all expenses for her education were borne. On the 17th of this month, my daughter stole a neighbor's rattan chair and brought it home. When it was discovered, I scolded her for not bringing other people's belongings into the house without permission. Unexpectedly, she had a habit of deceiving, and she secretly drank the "Sal," which was prepared for bathing. When it was discovered, she was immediately sent to the Dongyang Hospital for two emergency injections. According to the doctor, it had been too long, and the effect would likely be ineffective. Later, she was sent to the Guangdong Hospital for treatment, but she died. The whole family was very sad and speechless. There was no reason for abuse. I hereby declare the facts, hoping that you will publish them. Sincerely, Qiu Jinsheng, July 22nd.

Youth Corner

Our Dean of Students

— Bingxi

After reading Mr. Mumu's "Dean of Students", I couldn't help but smile. It's so strange. I thought our dean of students, Mr. Yi, was so unique. Who knew there would be someone just like him. Let me introduce him to you.

Mr. Yi is a new student returned from the United States. He is of moderate height and very thin. He sometimes wears a suit, sometimes a Chinese gown. Perhaps he thinks that a suit can express the youth's heroism, so whenever there are visiting guests or memorial meetings, he wears a very beautiful suit. Otherwise, he sometimes wears everything at once, like a fur robe or camel's hair robe. His face looks like he's sick, but he's very good at ball games. It's just a pity that his ears aren't doing their job.

I remember the first time he came to class, many of us happened to be late.

"No one is allowed to be late next time," he said with a straight face. "I think equality between men and women must be practiced everywhere, so I treat girls the same as boys. If any of you girls are dissatisfied with my strict policies, please don't come to class." As he spoke, he shot a sharp look at those of us who were late.

"He's so fierce," a voice came from the right corner of the classroom. Immediately, we all laughed.

"What are you laughing at?" he became even angrier. The whole room was silent immediately. Then he raised his voice and said,

"In America, students are not allowed to enter the classroom after the teacher..."

"American Students are much more polite to teachers than you..."

"Go and see an American School, and see if there is any laughter in the classroom..."

"Who taught this book last semester?" he asked after a moment.

"It was also someone who liked to talk about America," a student replied.

Then there was another burst of laughter.

"What's the matter?" he didn't hear the reason we were laughing.

Mr. Yi has a phonograph. He invites everyone to his bedroom to appreciate it, so his bedroom is like a marketplace. Every day after school, many people can be seen in his room. He proudly turns it on and explains,

"These records were all brought back from America..."

"It's America again," someone in the crowd always says with a sarcastic tone.

The most surprising thing is that one day he brought the phonograph to the classroom.

"These are some educational records I recently bought, so I'll let you all listen to them. It can improve your English," so he turned it on and on, not stopping until the end of class.

If we listen to educational records every time we go to class, won't we get tired of it? Therefore, we had to turn on movie records as well. He listened quietly, moving his feet back and forth, left and right, probably practicing dancing.

At that time, in the students' minds, Mr. Yi was suffering from a mental illness.

Mr. Yi is very nice to us girls. He invites you to eat, teaches you how to play ball, comes to your house to visit you... There's no end to it. If we have anything to bother him with, he never refuses.

"How old are you this year?"

"Do you have a boyfriend?"

"Social interaction between men and women here is too secretive..."

"The boys here have no personality..."

"We in America..."

These are all Mr. Yi's conversations with the girls, but one thing made us angry. When we heard that his tone with the boys was like this:

"Women are the most hateful and disgusting..." So his remarks are all inconsistent.

"He must have a mental illness."

"Li must have been dumped before."

These are the criticisms of him by many students.

Five Dollars

— Ying

One evening around 7:30 PM on the 11th, my family was sitting in the courtyard enjoying the cool air after dinner because of the hot weather. There were about a dozen of us. I was upstairs preparing to take a bath when a family member downstairs called out, "San Ying, there's a guest for you!" I rushed downstairs and saw a middle-aged woman I didn't recognize. I was surprised and asked her surname. She calmly told me her surname was Li, and that she was the elder sister of my classmate, the female athlete Li. She said the female athlete Li was her third younger sister. I invited her to sit down while I carefully observed her attire. She wore a bright green Indian qipao with slits up to a foot high, and high-heeled black leather shoes. She told me that her sister had informed her of everything about my school, such as how strict a certain director was, leaving almost no room for questions, and how the entire student body was dissatisfied with another director, but he was still hired for the next semester due to some reason. She even knew the short histories of each teacher, and even that the dormitory supervisor, Mr. Wu, had ugly handwriting and brought his child with him. She knew everything in detail. Moreover, she spoke fluent classical Chinese, saying things like, "It's best to avoid bad friends," and "One should stay away from people with improper behavior," and "At home, you rely on your parents; away from home, you rely on your teachers and friends," and so on.

Naively inexperienced in the ways of the world, I believed that everyone in society maintained their integrity, so I didn't doubt her and fully trusted that she was my classmate's sister. Later, I asked her the purpose of her visit. She furtively said, "I need to use the WC upstairs." This made me even more trusting, and I thought that was indeed her purpose, so I happily accompanied her upstairs and even let her wash her face. As she was leaving, she said to me, "Miss Wang, I'm embarrassed to say this, but I'm short of cash today and need to go to Nanjing on the 11 PM train. I'm short ten dollars. Could you lend me ten dollars?" I replied, "Let me ask my family if they have any."

So I discussed with my mother whether to lend her the money. My mother said, "She's probably a trickster. Don't lend it." But my vanity clouded my judgment, and I thought, "Surely I can't refuse to lend her a mere ten dollars? Wouldn't that be ridiculous? If it's real, how could I face my classmate, the female athlete Li?" So I advocated lending it. My mother said, "Then lend her five dollars, as if you're throwing it away." So I took a five-dollar bill upstairs and saw her staring intently at the two silver dollars my little brother was playing with, making clanging sounds. I handed her the money and said, "My mother just went out. I borrowed this from my aunt, so I only have five dollars. Is it enough?" She said, "I need about seven dollars." Haha, she was thinking about the two silver dollars my little brother had! I replied, "Just take a third-class seat then." She very politely said goodbye.

The story ends here, but the more I thought about it afterward, the more I suspected she was a con artist, but I couldn't say for sure. Well, it's been proven today. My classmate, Ms. Zhu, wrote to tell me she encountered a con artist and warned me to be careful. And according to the facts Ms. Zhu described, it was the exact same trick I had experienced, just with a slight variation. The con artist also said she needed to go to Nanjing and was short of cash. As a result, Ms. Zhu was also conned out of five dollars.
